### 6. Specific Issues  

Below are concrete issues, roughly in order of importance; “Lx” refers to approximate logical locations in the provided PDF snippets, not absolute line numbers. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/784d984c-ba65-4de4-9ab2-ea220b6d5a93/supplementary_main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYE5EAXOR6Q&Signature=NjyI%2FfCqzqoUGlFmmkHfGfN9F1E%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCICx6e59aRYRtiwvtnpYPBkgsXcXgwSapM6hSo%2BAOjwigAiA8P57gQ8FYtmlkYUmrni5iAZjv0kcTRT%2Bbuf1hcZzu3yrzBAgxEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIM1SoNYtiyZTvVY7g0KtAEmRhYGzDaAPFSSRzAuUrSL%2B2GpOZtmEsq1tu5SUgKCePNxjXaldesjbq8nm4Xhmfyw5qkjxYhIDWv1ljGBdAFq157nxGfPAR2Mr7DwI6FaoOFzQyFt798ZpC8KRC9alcT0cdGmVHOkIb6xdVQL%2BmlygNcmNLxyV%2FN9cgvXexkjs%2FQoq%2Fj0s1zwOvFTi%2FbtukhzO7hA303%2BlQEVqQjmSztVRTQ6OG6vmCZN2dzbl6RhOjg9nZsZEOSuviqc8%2Bv2uQd9wj6N5%2Bjdz8Poqe4Wy17w7dYciqhHnkjwsy1DvTst6Q%2Bfm0i67Nkbx8EDGHnkQEJmjoQM4qeXEoMcRDdvmaJMM6h2agQ9gzZqIq9E%2F1XN%2BMGPgqpdqdWIe6e4iiZBuxwvS7g6CzkfZhgM%2BWHG5rT2Dn3eieXW91PixM4d2%2FQM9%2BZSxzXRivHP6MWL26Ruoy%2Ff3HNwOs%2B8kVtWtXEnC2HtglWFJuZU2QwxVrEUe3bRk%2Bi654q%2BDj0KVrmsKuzVgxRo2gwnAjriW6gTHfIC49vj63Ns3GZe9dKw3%2Fbw9arCaEmtMWQ0fedkl%2B5qddD2ueD2Ki4m0JYUICkHIV8Vbc0xOGrGRQuWL3qOb%2BdFPf49dDp6a968LPFijLh%2BvM5vZUP3dCjlJNQT%2FpuYjUDX4xXemMtmJtOQjCzdnmJqDiYRigF%2F7GwbblVRUke7vvfanaWXiS7z9RCC7wYfJThj15THJMvHBZFPdUY%2F9jysztMlg17CdMU8trwzt6yIUwiJjmYMOUCA9UoGE7Z7PmmrTK%2B%2FTC3vuTOBjqZAQTN9g1B%2BqkeScM%2FIMvKlm1SQ8JL1aTp%2BmJTXnPPuBQT1uzKHU9f6254jWPrErwW%2BcQVFxLaMnfvYuvIHlU%2BUn4GRgwUbAFmfoDQgcYUlTEY82M6z01HKM8rZY2Qw2VcB7%2BR%2Bg8ZLk9fDMz5ZTWk%2BSxSOH3pmQqcumtmHwnsjOuEzawbqxU8Cw56hMjmNF3YJJXjMvpZHH1ATg%3D%3D&Expires=1775838108)

1. **Over-generalization of regime-specific findings**  
   - The statement that the uniform retention model is “validated” by comparison to a state-dependent model with <0.1 pp difference should be clearly labeled as specific to the V4 Ensemble HAT / CIFAR-10 regime; currently, it risks being read as a general statement about retention modeling sufficiency.    - Similarly, conclusions about C2C vs D2D importance (static D2D dominating C2C) are derived from a specific sensitivity sweep; the main text should emphasize that this is profile- and regime-dependent, not universal. 2. **Nonlinear write “hard boundary”**  
   - The main text calls the 27.72 ± 0.82% result under NL = 2.0 a hard boundary for the “current recipe,” but also notes elsewhere that the NL model is a gradient-scaling surrogate.  This should be rephrased consistently as: “hard boundary of the present surrogate and HAT recipe,” not of physical programming limits. 3. **Ensemble HAT characterization**  
   - Ensemble HAT is central to the claimed contribution (fresh-instance accuracy 86.37 ± 1.54%), yet its algorithmic details (e.g., number of D2D masks per epoch, whether masks are resampled per batch, per epoch, or per step; how many instances are seen during training) are not fully specified in the main text.    - The regularization/capacity trade-off is only qualitatively discussed; given its importance, a small ablation (e.g., number of instances vs accuracy vs training stability) would be valuable, or at least clearer documentation.  

4. **ADC modeling opacity**  
   - The 6-bit “cliff” is a key finding but the modeling of ADC non-idealities (noise, quantization, offset, gain error, INL/DNL) is not sufficiently described; the energy model also lumps ADC behaviorally without giving per-conversion parameters.  A table summarizing ADC model assumptions would help. 5. **Energy numbers and framing**  
   - The abstract and Figure 5 title present “11.45× lower than FP32” prominently; to avoid overstatement, they should explicitly say “11.45× lower in our analytical, first-order model” or similar, consistent with the careful language used later. 6. **Clarification of “scale masking”**  
   - The term “scale masking” is introduced but the mechanism (interaction of digital scale recovery, quantization, and noise) is only qualitatively described.  A concise mathematical explanation or illustrative toy example would make this more convincing. ### 8. Overall Recommendation  

**Recommendation: Major Revision**  

The manuscript addresses a timely and important problem—bridging organic optoelectronic synaptic devices and contemporary vision models via a profile-driven, hardware-aware simulator—and does so with a thoughtful, well-documented framework and a fairly extensive experimental campaign.  The transparency about modeling assumptions, the integration of ViTs and CNNs, and the explicit treatment of fresh-instance robustness and energy are significant strengths. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/784d984c-ba65-4de4-9ab2-ea220b6d5a93/supplementary_main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYE5EAXOR6Q&Signature=NjyI%2FfCqzqoUGlFmmkHfGfN9F1E%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCICx6e59aRYRtiwvtnpYPBkgsXcXgwSapM6hSo%2BAOjwigAiA8P57gQ8FYtmlkYUmrni5iAZjv0kcTRT%2Bbuf1hcZzu3yrzBAgxEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIM1SoNYtiyZTvVY7g0KtAEmRhYGzDaAPFSSRzAuUrSL%2B2GpOZtmEsq1tu5SUgKCePNxjXaldesjbq8nm4Xhmfyw5qkjxYhIDWv1ljGBdAFq157nxGfPAR2Mr7DwI6FaoOFzQyFt798ZpC8KRC9alcT0cdGmVHOkIb6xdVQL%2BmlygNcmNLxyV%2FN9cgvXexkjs%2FQoq%2Fj0s1zwOvFTi%2FbtukhzO7hA303%2BlQEVqQjmSztVRTQ6OG6vmCZN2dzbl6RhOjg9nZsZEOSuviqc8%2Bv2uQd9wj6N5%2Bjdz8Poqe4Wy17w7dYciqhHnkjwsy1DvTst6Q%2Bfm0i67Nkbx8EDGHnkQEJmjoQM4qeXEoMcRDdvmaJMM6h2agQ9gzZqIq9E%2F1XN%2BMGPgqpdqdWIe6e4iiZBuxwvS7g6CzkfZhgM%2BWHG5rT2Dn3eieXW91PixM4d2%2FQM9%2BZSxzXRivHP6MWL26Ruoy%2Ff3HNwOs%2B8kVtWtXEnC2HtglWFJuZU2QwxVrEUe3bRk%2Bi654q%2BDj0KVrmsKuzVgxRo2gwnAjriW6gTHfIC49vj63Ns3GZe9dKw3%2Fbw9arCaEmtMWQ0fedkl%2B5qddD2ueD2Ki4m0JYUICkHIV8Vbc0xOGrGRQuWL3qOb%2BdFPf49dDp6a968LPFijLh%2BvM5vZUP3dCjlJNQT%2FpuYjUDX4xXemMtmJtOQjCzdnmJqDiYRigF%2F7GwbblVRUke7vvfanaWXiS7z9RCC7wYfJThj15THJMvHBZFPdUY%2F9jysztMlg17CdMU8trwzt6yIUwiJjmYMOUCA9UoGE7Z7PmmrTK%2B%2FTC3vuTOBjqZAQTN9g1B%2BqkeScM%2FIMvKlm1SQ8JL1aTp%2BmJTXnPPuBQT1uzKHU9f6254jWPrErwW%2BcQVFxLaMnfvYuvIHlU%2BUn4GRgwUbAFmfoDQgcYUlTEY82M6z01HKM8rZY2Qw2VcB7%2BR%2Bg8ZLk9fDMz5ZTWk%2BSxSOH3pmQqcumtmHwnsjOuEzawbqxU8Cw56hMjmNF3YJJXjMvpZHH1ATg%3D%3D&Expires=1775838108)

However, for a Nature Communications publication, the current version overreaches slightly in the generality of some conclusions relative to the simplicity of the physical models and the limited quantitative validation against existing simulators or hardware. Several key claims—ADC bit-width limits, retention-model sufficiency, nonlinear write “hard boundaries,” and the generality of Ensemble HAT—require either stronger empirical support (more systematic sweeps and multi-seed studies) or more carefully scoped phrasing to make clear that they hold within the particular profiles and surrogates chosen.  Additional direct comparison against AIHWKIT/CrossSim and a more detailed characterization of Ensemble HAT would significantly enhance the paper’s credibility and impact. With these issues addressed, I believe the work could reach NC level as a simulation-centric, methodology-driven contribution that will be valuable to the organic neuromorphic and CIM communities.  

To help you prioritize revisions: is your primary goal for the next version to strengthen physical fidelity/validation, or to broaden the scope of models and datasets explored with the current simulator?

## gemini

### 1. Summary
[cite_start]The manuscript introduces a behavioral simulation framework designed to evaluate organic optoelectronic compute-in-memory (CIM) systems for edge vision workloads[cite: 342, 348]. [cite_start]By converting physical non-idealities derived from literature—such as quantization, device-to-device (D2D) and cycle-to-cycle (C2C) variability, retention drift, and nonlinear writing—into forward-pass perturbations, the framework assesses the performance of ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M backbones[cite: 349, 350]. [cite_start]The central finding is that nominal quantization is not the primary deployment bottleneck under hardware-aware training (HAT) [cite: 351][cite_start]; rather, system viability is severely gated by ADC resolution, fresh-instance transferability, and complex write nonlinearities[cite: 352, 353].

### 2. Significance & Novelty
* [cite_start]**Addressing a Meaningful Gap:** The work successfully identifies and bridges a critical gap between low-level materials characterization of organic synapses and the system-level realities of deploying modern vision transformers[cite: 361, 363, 366]. 
* [cite_start]**Methodological Contribution:** The primary contribution is methodological[cite: 375]. [cite_start]Extending traditional CIM simulation paradigms to natively support organic-specific phenomena—specifically inverse-gamma optical frontend compensation and profile substitution—provides a valuable new tool for the community[cite: 365, 377].
* [cite_start]**Comparison to Existing Frameworks:** The authors correctly identify that mature simulators like DNN+NeuroSim and CrossSim are heavily optimized for inorganic resistive memories (e.g., ReRAM, PCM)[cite: 398, 399, 400]. [cite_start]Highlighting the distinct multimodal (optoelectronic) tuning and severe nonlinear write asymmetry of organic devices justifies the need for this specialized framework[cite: 193, 194].
* **Suitability for Nature Communications:** The paper is highly relevant to the journal's applied physics and materials engineering audience. [cite_start]However, because it is a purely simulation-based study lacking novel device fabrication, the physical validity of its simulated assumptions must be absolutely rigorous to meet the venue's threshold for impact[cite: 371, 460].

### 3. Technical Soundness
* [cite_start]**Physical Assumptions:** Grounding the simulation parameters in recent literature, such as the 2026 OPECT profile by Zhang et al. and retention dynamics from Vincze et al., is a strong approach that validates the "profile-driven" claims[cite: 34, 38, 354]. 
* [cite_start]**Device-to-System Mapping:** The translation of weights to bounded differential conductances, combined with straight-through estimator (STE) gradient scaling for nonlinear writes, is mathematically sound[cite: 434, 435, 64, 65, 73]. 
* [cite_start]**Statistical Rigor:** The use of 10-run Monte Carlo sweeps to evaluate stochastic forward passes is appropriate[cite: 18, 29]. [cite_start]The explicit tracking of seeds for reproducibility is also commendable[cite: 575]. 
* [cite_start]**Potential Issues (Energy & Scaling):** The assumption that post-array scale recovery acts as an "ideal calibrated digital rescaling" step is highly optimistic[cite: 436, 437]. Real-world ADC nonlinearities and offset errors often corrupt this calibration. [cite_start]Consequently, the claim that digital rescaling effectively masks nominal conductance noise ("Scale Masking") may be an artifact of this idealized assumption[cite: 555]. [cite_start]Furthermore, absorbing all interconnect and routing overhead into generic SRAM access terms yields an 11.45x efficiency claim that functions strictly as an absolute upper bound, which risks misleading readers about actual chip-level power savings[cite: 582, 583, 666, 667].

### 4. Presentation & Narrative
* **Story Arc:** The narrative flow is logical and compelling. [cite_start]It transitions smoothly from the overarching device-to-system deployment gap to specific methodological implementations, followed by stress-testing physical bottlenecks[cite: 361, 366, 367].
* [cite_start]**Abstract:** The abstract is precise and accurately reflects the core quantitative findings, particularly the drastic recovery enabled by Ensemble HAT[cite: 353, 355].
* [cite_start]**Figures and Formatting:** Figure 5 provides an excellent, transparent breakdown of the energy distribution, clearly illustrating the "analog ceiling" imposed by digital attention mechanisms[cite: 617, 657, 658]. [cite_start]The qualitative attention heatmaps in Supplementary Figure S3 are effectively corroborated by the quantitative entropy metrics discussed in the text[cite: 227, 619, 620].
* [cite_start]**Document Length:** Offloading the detailed parameter provenance and sensitivity sweeps to the Supplementary Information prevents the main text from becoming a dense methods manual, which suits the formatting constraints of the journal[cite: 24, 465].

### 5. Missing References or Comparisons
* [cite_start]**Inorganic Comparisons:** Supplementary Figure S2 directly compares the organic profiles against inorganic PCM and ReRAM benchmarks[cite: 154, 157, 176]. [cite_start]Given that a major selling point of the manuscript is contextualizing organic devices against mature inorganic technologies[cite: 191, 192], burying this direct comparison in the SI weakens the paper. This figure and the accompanying analysis should be promoted to the main text.

### 6. Specific Issues
* [cite_start]**C2C Sensitivity Artifacts:** In Table S3, the maximum accuracy excursion across the full C2C sweep is reported as exactly 0.00 percentage points[cite: 47, 50]. [cite_start]While the authors note this is a stability result[cite: 51], it suggests that C2C noise is being entirely eclipsed by quantization binning or D2D mismatch. This dynamic requires a deeper mechanistic explanation in the main text.
* [cite_start]**Flowers-102 Baseline:** The FP32 digital baseline for ConvNeXt-Tiny on the Flowers-102 dataset is reported as 33.22%[cite: 455]. This is exceptionally low for a standard CNN. [cite_start]If the base model fails to converge cleanly in the digital domain, using it to diagnose analog noise failures ("data starvation hypothesis") introduces significant confounding variables[cite: 653, 654].
* [cite_start]**Array Non-Idealities Penalty:** The authors admit that IR drop and sneak-path currents are excluded, citing an expected 1-3% accuracy drop based on ReRAM literature[cite: 673, 674, 675]. However, organic semiconducting arrays frequently exhibit much higher line resistances than metallic ReRAM crossbars. Applying a 1-3% inorganic penalty proxy to an organic simulation is likely a severe underestimation.

### 7. Questions for Authors
1.  [cite_start]How robust is the "Scale Masking" phenomenon when the "ideal calibrated digital rescaling" assumption is relaxed[cite: 436, 555]? Have you simulated the impact of realistic ADC offset errors or nonlinearities on this calibration step?
2.  [cite_start]In Table S3, the C2C noise appears to have literally zero impact on accuracy (0.00 percentage points variance) at a fixed D2D mismatch[cite: 47, 50]. Is this entirely an artifact of the 4-bit quantization grid absorbing the perturbations, and if so, at what C2C variance does this masking effect finally break?
3.  [cite_start]Why are the direct accuracy comparisons between organic profiles and inorganic PCM/ReRAM baselines relegated to Supplementary Figure S2[cite: 154, 157]? 
4.  [cite_start]Given that organic materials typically suffer from higher sheet resistances than inorganic equivalents, is the 1-3% accuracy degradation estimate for unmodeled IR drops (drawn from ReRAM literature) physically realistic for your proposed organic arrays[cite: 673, 675]?
5.  [cite_start]How can we confidently assess analog noise robustness on the Flowers-102 dataset when the digital FP32 ConvNeXt-Tiny baseline only achieves 33.22%[cite: 455]? 

### 8. Overall Recommendation
**Major Revision**

The manuscript presents a timely, well-engineered, and highly relevant simulation framework that brings much-needed system-level rigorousness to the evaluation of organic neuromorphic devices. The inclusion of optoelectronic frontend distortion and Ensemble HAT are notable highlights. However, as a purely simulation-driven paper, its impact hinges on the validity of its physical constraints. The reliance on ideal digital scale recovery, the un-modeled interconnect energy overhead, and the application of inorganic IR-drop proxies to organic arrays currently paint an overly optimistic picture of deployment readiness. Addressing these specific idealizations—and moving the vital inorganic baseline comparisons into the main text—will ensure the framework serves as a reliable, rather than purely aspirational, tool for the community.

## gpt

I reviewed the main manuscript and Supplementary Information.  

# Reviewer #2 Report

## 1. Summary

This manuscript presents a **profile-driven, first-order behavioral simulation framework** for evaluating organic optoelectronic compute-in-memory (CIM) inference on edge-vision workloads. The framework maps literature-derived or measured device assumptions into task-level accuracy and energy trends for hybrid analog/digital deployments of ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M, with particular emphasis on quantization, D2D/C2C variability, retention, ADC precision, optical frontend distortion, and nonlinear write effects. The central claim is that, in the studied regime, **quantization alone is not the dominant bottleneck**; instead, ADC precision, task complexity, fresh-instance transfer, and richer physical effects dominate deployment risk, while Ensemble HAT partially rescues fresh-instance generalization. The authors position the tool not as a chip-predictive emulator, but as a transparent materials-to-system bridge for organic optoelectronic CIM.  

## 2. Significance & Novelty

This work addresses a **real gap**. The manuscript is correct that much of the organic optoelectronic synapse literature remains device-centric, while mainstream CIM tools are largely organized around inorganic memories rather than organic profile substitution, optical frontends, and hybrid ViT deployment. That gap is meaningful for the neuromorphic/CIM community. 

That said, the contribution is **primarily methodological**, with simulation experiments serving as demonstrations rather than as independent validation. The novelty is not a fundamentally new analog-CIM simulator kernel on the level of NeuroSim, CrossSim, or AIHWKIT. Rather, it is an **integration layer** that combines:

* organic-device profile substitution,
* optoelectronic frontend distortion modeling,
* hybrid operator mapping for Tiny-ViT, and
* hardware-aware retraining/stress testing in a PyTorch workflow.  

Relative to AIHWKIT, CrossSim, and NeuroSim, the manuscript’s differentiator is therefore **domain specialization**, not simulator fidelity. The paper itself acknowledges that IR drop, sneak paths, differential-branch asymmetry, optical crosstalk, temperature effects, and pulse-faithful programming are out of scope. That is acceptable for a first-order tool, but it also means the framework is **less physically grounded** than those mature platforms in several dimensions, especially at the array/peripheral level.  

For **Nature Communications**, I am less convinced. The topic is certainly of interest to NC readers working at the materials-device-system interface, but the current manuscript does not yet clear the validation bar expected for NC. In its present form, it reads more like a strong **simulation/co-design methods paper** than a decisive advance in experimentally anchored organic neuromorphic hardware. With substantially stronger validation and statistical rigor, it could become competitive; as submitted, it feels **borderline for NC and more naturally suited to a specialist device/system venue**.  

## 3. Technical Soundness

### Overall assessment

The framework is **technically coherent as a first-order behavioral simulator**, and the authors are more transparent than many papers in explicitly labeling assumptions, proxies, and out-of-scope effects. That transparency is a strength. However, the paper still overreaches at several points when turning those simulations into deployment-facing conclusions.  

### Major strengths

* The authors do not hide the fact that the study is simulation-only, literature-derived, and proxy-calibrated. 
* The manuscript distinguishes same-instance robustness from fresh-instance transfer, and the Ensemble HAT result is one of the strongest and most useful observations in the paper.  
* The Supplementary Information is unusually explicit about parameter provenance and evaluation protocol.  

### Major concerns

#### 3.1 Simulation assumptions remain only weakly validated

The core “profile-driven” claim is not yet validated strongly enough. The Zhang OPECT case study is based on **proxy estimates** for noise and incomplete fitting for retention, with the Supplementary Information explicitly stating that some values are proxy estimates or analytical assumptions and that Zhang retention is “not fitted.” That is acceptable as an exploratory case study, but not as strong evidence that the framework can reliably convert device literature into deployment predictions. 

I would urge the authors to separate much more sharply:

1. what is **directly constrained by measurements**,
2. what is **proxy-derived**, and
3. what is **pure simulator extrapolation**.

At present these categories blur together, especially in the abstract and conclusions.  

#### 3.2 Device-to-system mapping is plausible but too idealized

The differential conductance mapping is described as bounded, quantized, and perturbed, with **ideal calibrated digital post-processing** for scale recovery and no explicit modeling of systematic positive/negative branch asymmetry. The Supplementary Information further notes that any implied common-mode cancellation is a simplifying assumption. This is a major idealization because the manuscript’s central “scale-masking” interpretation may depend materially on those ideal recovery assumptions.  

The paper needs much clearer, equation-level exposition of:

* how floating-point weights are normalized into ([G_{\min}, G_{\max}]),
* how sign/differential coding is handled layerwise,
* how clipping/saturation are treated,
* how post-array scale recovery is calibrated, and
* what exact calibration burden is assumed at deployment.  

#### 3.3 Experimental controls are not yet NC-grade

The most serious methodological problem is in the evaluation protocol: the Supplementary Information states that for each training run the authors **record the best test accuracy across epochs** and save checkpoints for later sweeps. That is not a minor presentation issue; it is a model-selection issue. Test data should not be used to choose the best epoch. A validation split should select checkpoints, and test performance should be reported once. As written, reported headline numbers are optimistic. 

Relatedly, the Supplementary Information states that the **full multi-seed campaign is still being accumulated**, and only a single fresh rerun is offered as a sanity check for the canonical V4 path. This is not sufficient for a paper making broad claims about robustness and deployment risk. 

The statistical treatment also mixes different sources of variability:

* some error bars reflect **Monte Carlo inference noise on a fixed checkpoint**,
* others partially reflect **fresh hardware instances**,
* but training-seed variability is largely missing for the main Tiny-ViT claims.  

Those are not interchangeable uncertainty measures.

#### 3.4 Retention modeling is under-validated

The paper claims that corrected V4 results validate uniform decay sufficiency for the present regime, and the Supplementary Information reports <0.1 pp difference between uniform and state-dependent retention. However, the same Supplementary section explicitly states that this comparison was performed **only on the retained Ensemble-HAT path**, not on the collapsing fresh-instance path or non-HAT checkpoints, and should not be read as universal. That limitation is important and should move from SI into the main text. 

Given that retention is a central claimed differentiator of organic devices, the retention section currently feels too narrow for the weight placed on it in the manuscript’s framing. 

#### 3.5 Noise injection semantics need tighter justification

The paper considers both “uniform” and “proportional” noise semantics. The latter is more physical; the former is a convenient normalized stress model. But the manuscript makes several conclusions from the canonical uniform setting, then later shows that those conclusions do not survive under proportional noise. That is acceptable if framed correctly, but the current framing still makes the canonical result sound more general than it is.  

Table S3 is also concerning: the rows are numerically identical across the entire C2C sweep. The authors explain this as a real stability result, not a copy-paste error, but it remains surprising enough that I would want to see:

* higher precision,
* raw run distributions,
* and possibly a unit-test-like verification that C2C noise is actually being injected as intended in that sweep. 

#### 3.6 ADC modeling and energy modeling are not yet convincing enough

The paper argues that ADC precision is the dominant bottleneck, with a 6-bit cliff in accuracy, yet the energy breakdown assigns **<0.1%** of hybrid energy to ADC and DAC while digital attention dominates the budget. This is not impossible, but it is counterintuitive enough that the model needs substantially more explanation. How can converter precision be the central accuracy bottleneck while converter energy is effectively negligible? Are these results driven by quantizer saturation, transfer nonlinearity, clipping, range setting, or some other modeling choice?  

The energy claims are also too soft to support strong conclusions:

* buffer cost is explicitly “not modeled”;
* scale recovery overhead is absorbed ideally;
* routing/interconnect is only sensitivity-tested;
* the digital baseline is FP32 from a Horowitz-style estimate, not a matched modern edge baseline.  

So the energy analysis is useful as a rough directional argument, but it is not strong enough to support a headline “11.45×” message in a high-impact venue.

## 4. Presentation & Narrative

The paper’s **story arc is clear**: there is a materials-to-system gap; the authors offer a profile-driven simulator; they probe which non-idealities matter; they conclude that transfer, converter precision, and richer physical laws dominate over simple quantization. Structurally, that arc works. 

The **abstract is well written**, but slightly over-assertive given the evidence. In particular, phrases implying that literature characterization can already be turned into deployment-oriented evaluation should be softened because the current case study still depends heavily on proxy assumptions.  

The figures are generally readable, but I would streamline them:

* **Figure 1** is useful.
* **Figure 2** is conceptually important but should include clearer operator semantics and perhaps one minimal equation.
* **Figures 3–4** are central and appropriate.
* **Figure 5** is helpful, but the “buffer not modeled” presentation undercuts interpretability.
* **Supplementary Figure S2** includes representative CIFAR images that add little.
* **Supplementary Figure S3** attention maps are visually suggestive but statistically weak; the added entropy numbers on three samples do not fully rescue them.  

Length is acceptable for NC, but the manuscript is **imbalanced**:

* the Discussion is somewhat expansive,
* while the Methods/main-text physical model description is too compressed,
* forcing several important caveats into the Supplementary Information.  

## 5. Missing References or Comparisons

The paper cites the right broad families of work, but the **comparative analysis is shallow**. The main missing elements are not necessarily missing citations as much as **missing matched comparisons**.

The authors should strengthen comparison against:

1. **AIHWKIT / CrossSim / NeuroSim under matched settings**, beyond the very limited supplementary AIHWKIT sanity check on a 256-sample subset. That comparison is too small to establish meaningful numerical consistency. 
2. **Recent ViT-on-CIM / ViT-on-PIM deployment studies**, especially those that discuss which operators remain digital, quantization sensitivity of attention blocks, and mixed-signal partitioning. The manuscript cites some ViT quantization papers and PIM references, but the comparative discussion remains thin. 
3. **Measured organic array / in-sensor computing studies** with quantified non-idealities. The paper cites several relevant array papers, but the bridge from those measurements to simulator parameters remains mostly qualitative. 
4. **Calibration / inference-on-measured-device-profile papers**. Since “profile substitution” is the central differentiator, the manuscript would benefit from stronger engagement with literature on fitting measured device statistics into system-level simulators. 

## 6. Specific Issues

Below are concrete manuscript-level issues.

1. **Internal inconsistency in baseline numbers.**
   Table 1 reports Tiny-ViT CIFAR-10 at **97.48%**, while Section 5.1 states **98.06%**. Table 1 also reports ResNet-18 CIFAR-10 at **94.98%**, whereas Table 2 lists **94.88%**; ConvNeXt-Tiny CIFAR-10 is **90.74%** in Table 1 but **90.17%** in Table 2. These must be reconciled.  

2. **Checkpoint selection on the test set.**
   The SI states that the best **test** accuracy across epochs is recorded. This is not acceptable as written and materially affects the credibility of the reported gains. 

3. **Incomplete seed statistics for headline claims.**
   The SI acknowledges that the full multi-seed campaign is still incomplete. That is incompatible with strong robustness claims in the main manuscript. 

4. **Single-run estimate in Table 1 is under-signaled.**
   The ConvNeXt–Flowers-102 baseline is marked as a single-run estimate in Table 1, but the downstream discussion does not foreground that fragility sufficiently. 

5. **Overstatement of “deployment-facing” conclusions.**
   Because all device parameters are literature-derived or proxy-calibrated and physical validation is future work, several statements in the abstract/discussion should be softened. 

6. **Retention claim should be narrowed.**
   The SI explicitly says the uniform-vs-state-dependent check is regime-specific and not universal. The main text should say so. 

7. **Table S3 requires stronger verification.**
   Identical rows across the C2C sweep are surprising enough that raw data or higher-precision statistics should be shown. 

8. **The Zhang profile case study is only partially fitted.**
   Noise values are proxy-estimated, retention is not fitted, and some values are analytical assumptions. This should be much more prominent in the case-study narrative. 

9. **ADC bottleneck vs ADC energy needs reconciliation.**
   The manuscript simultaneously argues that ADC precision is the key accuracy bottleneck and that ADC energy is negligible. The modeling assumptions behind this should be explicit.  

10. **Energy comparison baseline is weak.**
    The “11.45×” comparison to an FP32 estimate is not the strongest or most relevant deployment baseline for edge vision. At minimum, a matched digital low-precision baseline should be reported. 

11. **Architecture comparison is confounded.**
    Tiny-ViT is fine-tuned from ImageNet; ConvNeXt is trained from scratch. The paper acknowledges complementary roles, but some CNN-vs-ViT comparisons still read too categorically.  

12. **Array size / mapping granularity are insufficiently explicit.**
    Since limitations discuss IR drop beyond (>256\times256), the actual layer-to-array mapping assumptions should be stated more clearly in the main methods. 

13. **The AIHWKIT comparison is too weak.**
    A five-run comparison on a fixed 256-sample subset is not enough to substantiate numerical consistency with a mature simulator. 

14. **Formatting issue:** the main text appears to contain a literal markdown-style bold entry “**84.75 ± 0.72%**”. This should be cleaned. 

15. **Figure S3 is not yet publication-grade evidence.**
    Three representative attention maps plus a three-sample entropy summary are too anecdotal for the argumentative weight currently placed on them. 

## 7. Questions for Authors

1. **Checkpoint selection:** Did the authors truly select the best epoch using the test set, as stated in the SI? If so, can all headline numbers be recomputed using a proper validation-set selection protocol? 

2. **Profile validation:** What concrete evidence supports the claim that the profile-substitution interface can produce quantitatively meaningful deployment predictions, rather than only exploratory trend analyses, when several case-study parameters are proxy-estimated or unfitted? 

3. **ADC model:** What exact ADC transfer model was used in the accuracy sweeps—range setting, clipping, DNL/INL parameterization, per-layer calibration, and full-scale assumptions—and how does that model explain the strong accuracy sensitivity but negligible energy contribution?  

4. **Noise semantics:** Why are the Table S3 results completely invariant to the full C2C sweep at reported precision? Can the authors provide raw distributions or a sensitivity audit to exclude implementation artifacts? 

5. **Generalization claims:** How robust are the main Tiny-ViT conclusions across training seeds, given that the SI states the multi-seed campaign is incomplete? 

## 8. Overall Recommendation

**Recommendation: Major Revision**

This is an intelligent, potentially useful manuscript with a clear niche: it attempts to bridge organic optoelectronic device characterization and modern vision-model deployment through a profile-driven CIM simulator. The manuscript’s strengths are its transparent scoping, its focus on fresh-instance transfer rather than only same-instance robustness, and its effort to treat organic-specific frontend and retention effects inside a modern ML workflow. However, several issues prevent acceptance in the present form: the use of best test accuracy across epochs, incomplete seed statistics for headline claims, reliance on proxy-calibrated parameters for the central case study, insufficient validation of the “profile-driven” premise, and an energy story that is informative but too idealized for strong conclusions. I would encourage a substantially revised version, but for **Nature Communications** specifically, the paper is **not yet sufficiently validated or statistically mature**. The clearest path forward is to tighten experimental protocol, expand seed-based statistics, sharpen the boundary between simulation and evidence, and provide much stronger matched validation against measured profiles and/or established simulators.

## claude

This is a rich manuscript — I'll dive into a thorough review. Let me research the current state of organic CIM simulation frameworks, recent ViT-on-hardware papers, and the cited references to ground my assessment properly.Your peer review briefing for "Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic CIM Inference" is ready. It covers verification of the two cited organic device papers, a critical finding that the retention parameters likely conflate short-term plasticity decay with CIM weight retention, assessment of the composite device profile, confirmation that no existing CIM framework supports organic devices, evaluation of the ensemble HAT novelty and the unusually large accuracy recovery claim, contextualization of the 11.45× energy reduction against hardware demonstrations, and identification of approximately 20 missing references spanning CIM simulators with ViT support, hardware-aware training methods, and recent organic neuromorphic reviews.

# Peer review background for "Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic CIM Inference"

**The manuscript addresses a genuine gap — bridging organic optoelectronic device profiles with system-level DNN inference simulation — but several critical issues with physical parameter interpretation, experimental grounding, and missing contextual citations substantially weaken the claims.** The paper's most novel contribution (ensemble HAT for organic CIM) appears to lack direct precedent, and the device parameter profile draws on sources whose physical context may be misrepresented. Below is a detailed research briefing across all seven requested areas to inform a rigorous review.

---

## Both cited organic device papers are real but raise red flags when used as CIM parameters

**Liu et al. (Nature Communications 17, 197, 2026)** is confirmed published (DOI: 10.1038/s41467-025-66891-6). It reports NIR organic photoelectrochemical transistors (OPECTs) fabricated via wafer-scale photolithography at Tongji University. Key metrics: **Gmax/Gmin >2,379** (600 optical pulses), ultra-low write nonlinearity (NL = −0.015), **34 distinguishable conductance states** with retention exceeding 1,000 seconds, and Vth uniformity of 0.5–1% across 80 devices. The device achieves 93.29% MNIST accuracy in a simulated CNN. This paper demonstrates that state-of-the-art organic OPECTs dramatically exceed the Gmax/Gmin = 10 and 4-bit (16-state) parameters used in the manuscript under review — meaning the manuscript's parameter choices are conservative relative to the best reported devices, which is defensible but should be acknowledged explicitly.

**Vincze et al. (Advanced Electronic Materials 12(1), 2026)** is confirmed published (DOI: 10.1002/aelm.202500515). It reports a DNTT-based organic FET demonstrating simultaneous short-term and long-term plasticity under optical stimulation. **The critical issue: the device operates at 200 K (−73°C), not room temperature**, and was designed for potential space-based neuromorphic systems (Mars surface conditions). The paper reports paired-pulse facilitation (PPF) with **τ₁ = 140 ± 11 ms and τ₂ = 610 ± 73 ms** — these are the exact values used as retention parameters in the manuscript under review.

**This constitutes the most serious concern for reviewers.** The τ₁ and τ₂ values from Vincze et al. characterize **short-term synaptic plasticity decay** (how quickly paired-pulse facilitation fades after two rapid stimuli), not **weight retention** in the CIM sense (how long a programmed conductance state persists). In CIM inference, retention refers to the temporal stability of programmed weights during computation — a fundamentally different physical process. Actual weight retention in organic synaptic devices ranges from **60 seconds to >1,000 seconds** for properly programmed LTP states (Liu et al. report >1,000 s; Shan et al. 2026 report 82% retention at 1,000 s across 5 states). Using sub-second PPF decay constants as CIM retention parameters would dramatically overstate the severity of retention loss during inference, since even a millisecond-scale inference latency would imply catastrophic weight decay that real organic LTP states do not exhibit. The manuscript should clarify whether it models STP-regime operation (a niche scenario) or has conflated PPF dynamics with weight retention.

## The other device parameters are individually reasonable but assembled from heterogeneous sources

The parameter profile used in the manuscript — **Gmax/Gmin = 10, 4-bit states, σC2C = 5%, σD2D = 10%** — draws from a patchwork of different device studies and conditions. Each parameter falls within reported ranges for organic synaptic transistors:

- **Gmax/Gmin = 10** is at the low end of literature values (range: 1.68 for basic CIG-OSTs to >2,379 for optimized OPECTs), and has been cited as the minimum threshold for useful ANN computation. A Nature Communications GIFET paper explicitly identifies Gmax/Gmin ≈ 10 as an on/off ratio target for high ANN performance.
- **4-bit / 16 states** is well within demonstrated capabilities: Wang et al. (Nature Electronics 2023) achieved **10-bit (1,024 states)** in OECTs; Liu et al. achieved 34 states; heterojunction OSPs achieved 800 states.
- **σC2C = 5%** is moderate: Won et al. (Advanced Functional Materials 2026) report **0.96%** for anion-excessive gel OSTs, while less optimized devices show 2–10%.
- **σD2D = 10%** is typical for organic transistor arrays fabricated via spin-coating and photolithography (range: 5–15%). Liu et al.'s wafer-scale OPECT array shows Vth variability of only 0.5–1%, though conductance variability would be higher.

The concern is not that individual parameters are unreasonable, but that **no single organic device simultaneously exhibits all these characteristics under identical operating conditions**. The profile is a composite, and the manuscript should explicitly state this, discuss parameter correlations (e.g., higher Gmax/Gmin ratios often come with worse nonlinearity), and present sensitivity analyses across the parameter space rather than treating one composite profile as representative.

## No existing CIM framework supports organic devices — the gap is real but cuts both ways

**AIHWKIT** (IBM, v1.0.0, May 2025) supports PCM and ReRAM with calibrated noise models. **CrossSim** (Sandia, v3.1, January 2025) uses lookup tables from experimental device data — all documented examples use inorganic NVM. **DNN+NeuroSim** (Georgia Tech, v1.5, 2025) supports SRAM, RRAM, PCM, STT-MRAM, FeFET, and nvCap. **MemTorch** (v1.0, 2022) supports five RRAM models with an extensible base class. **None of these frameworks include organic device models or presets.** The organic neuromorphic community uses fundamentally different simulation approaches: physics-based OECT models (drift-diffusion), SPICE-level compact models, and Hodgkin-Huxley-inspired neural circuit models — none integrated into DNN inference frameworks.

This confirms the manuscript's contribution addresses a genuine gap. However, this same gap means **there is no established methodology for validating organic CIM simulation against hardware**, unlike inorganic CIM simulators that are regularly validated against fabricated crossbar arrays (e.g., NeuroSim v1.5 validated against 40nm RRAM macro with <1% chip-level error). The manuscript should acknowledge this validation deficit explicitly and discuss what experimental measurements would be needed to validate its predictions.

**Critically, DNN+NeuroSim V1.5 (arXiv:2505.02314, 2025) now includes explicit Vision Transformer support** via a hybrid ACIM/DCIM architecture, with ViT-specific findings showing that **attention layers exhibit 1.25× higher RMSE than non-attention layers** and that Swin-T has significantly lower noise tolerance than ResNet-50. This is directly relevant and likely contemporaneous work that should be cited and compared against.

## Ensemble HAT appears genuinely novel, but the accuracy claims need careful scrutiny

No prior work was found on ensemble hardware-aware training — training multiple models with different device-to-device noise samples and ensembling predictions. The closest conceptual relatives are: (1) IBM's AIHWKIT noise injection during training (re-sampling noise per mini-batch, not per model); (2) ASiM framework's majority voting for CIM robustness; (3) multi-teacher robust distillation for memristor CIM non-idealities. The novelty claim appears supported.

The key benchmark paper is **Rasch et al. (Nature Communications 14, 5282, 2023)**, which demonstrated hardware-aware training across CNNs, RNNs, and transformers (including BERT) on PCM-calibrated models, achieving iso-accuracy with floating-point. More recently, **Liu et al. (Nature Communications 16, 2025)** proposed error-aware probabilistic training (EaPU) validated on ResNet and Vision Transformers, achieving **60%+ accuracy improvement** over naive deployment. **Chen et al. (Nature Communications, 2025)** demonstrated ALBERT on IBM's 14nm analog chip with HWA fine-tuning contributing **4.4% average accuracy improvement**. A paper on noise-aware knowledge distillation for RRAM-based ViTs (IEEE 2025) found earlier transformer layers more vulnerable and achieved up to 1.54% accuracy improvement.

The manuscript's claim that ensemble HAT raises fresh-instance Tiny-ViT accuracy from **10% to 86.37 ± 1.54%** deserves scrutiny. A 76-percentage-point recovery is extraordinarily large compared to the 1.5–4.4% improvements reported for HAT in inorganic CIM papers. This suggests either: (a) the baseline (fresh instance without HAT) is catastrophically poor because the organic device profile is unusually harsh, (b) the ensemble approach is exceptionally effective, or (c) the simulation setup may not be comparable to prior HAT studies. The 10% baseline for Tiny-ViT (essentially random on CIFAR-10) implies complete model collapse under the organic noise profile — reviewers should ask whether this reflects realistic operating conditions or an artificially pessimistic parameter regime.

## The 11.45× energy reduction is plausible as an upper bound but requires careful baseline specification

Typical energy estimates for analog CIM versus digital baselines from the literature:

- **IBM 14nm PCM chip (2023)**: 14× improvement for RNNT speech model at system level; tiles achieve ~20 TOPS/W
- **IBM ALBERT on 14nm analog chip (2025)**: Only **3–4× tile-level efficiency** over 14nm digital; ~3 TOPS/W system-level for GLUE tasks
- **Analog/digital hybrid attention accelerator**: **12.9× energy savings** over 8-bit fully digital for transformer attention (without pruning)
- **Xpikeformer (spiking transformer on RRAM CIM)**: **17.8–19.2× energy reduction** vs. digital ANN transformers
- **NeuroSim V1.5 findings**: ViTs are more sensitive to analog noise than CNNs, potentially requiring higher precision (and thus lower energy efficiency)

The **273.94 µJ** per inference and **11.45×** reduction claim falls within the plausible range for a simulated upper bound. However, the actual IBM hardware demonstrations show much more modest improvements for transformers (3–4×), suggesting that simulated projections tend to be optimistic. Key questions for reviewers: What is the digital baseline? (FP32 GPU? INT8 ASIC? What architecture and process node?) Does the energy model account for ADC/DAC overhead, data movement, and peripheral circuitry? Is it MAC-only or full-system? The **I-ViT paper** (Li & Gu, ICCV 2023) provides INT8 ViT baselines with 3.72–4.11× speedup on GPU but focuses on latency rather than explicit energy numbers — it provides software quantization efficiency, not hardware energy.

## Nature Communications has simulation-only CIM precedent, but the bar is high

The clearest precedent is **Rasch et al. (Nature Communications 14, 5282, 2023)** — a predominantly simulation-based paper using AIHWKIT to systematically examine DNN accuracy across convnets, RNNs, and transformers under analog non-idealities. It achieved 135+ citations and was accepted because: (a) device models were **calibrated against real experimental PCM/ReRAM data**, (b) the framework was open-source and well-established, (c) the study provided broad systematic insights not achievable with current hardware, and (d) results were validated across multiple architectures. **Rasch et al. 2024** (Nature Communications 15, 7137) is similarly simulation-heavy.

However, the **overwhelming norm** for Nature Communications CIM papers is experimental hardware: full-stack memristor systems (2025), memristor-based adaptive ADC (2025), solar-powered memristor BNN (2024), fabricated ASICs (2024). A purely simulation-based paper on organic CIM would need to demonstrate that its device models are grounded in measured data — the composite parameter profile assembled from different papers under different conditions may not meet this standard. The IBM precedent used models calibrated on a single device platform (PCM) with millions of measured devices. The manuscript's use of parameters drawn from Liu et al. (OPECTs at room temperature) and Vincze et al. (DNTT OFETs at 200K) creates a less coherent device profile.

## Important missing references and contextual gaps

Several 2024–2026 papers are directly relevant but may be missing:

**CIM simulation frameworks and ViT-on-CIM:**
- NeuroSim V1.5 (arXiv:2505.02314, 2025) — first major CIM simulator with explicit ViT support; directly comparable methodology
- TrilinearCIM (arXiv:2604.07628, 2025) — DG-FeFET architecture for transformer attention entirely in-memory
- Hemlet (arXiv:2511.15397, 2025) — heterogeneous CIM chiplet architecture specifically for ViTs
- CiMLoop (arXiv:2405.07259, 2024) — validated device-circuit-architecture CIM modeling tool
- MNSIM 2.0 (IEEE TCAD, 2023) — explicitly described as "behavior-level modeling tool" for CIM

**Hardware-aware training:**
- Liu et al., "Error-aware probabilistic training for memristive neural networks" (Nature Communications 16, 2025) — EaPU validated on ViTs
- Chen et al., "Demonstration of transformer-based ALBERT model on a 14nm analog AI inference chip" (Nature Communications, 2025) — first large transformer on analog hardware
- AIHWKIT-Lightning (NeurIPS 2024) — scalable HWA training up to 3.8B parameters
- RAOQ (ICML 2024) — quantization-aware training specifically targeting ADC quantization in IMC for ViTs

**ViT quantization:**
- APHQ-ViT (CVPR 2025), ERQ (ICML 2024), H-ViT (2025) — PTQ/QAT methods for ViTs relevant to CIM precision constraints
- Du et al., "Model Quantization and Hardware Acceleration for Vision Transformers: A Comprehensive Survey" (arXiv:2405.00314, 2024)

**Organic neuromorphic reviews (2025–2026):**
- Kim, "The Rise of Organic Electrochemical Transistors for Brain-Inspired Neuromorphic Computing" (Advanced Electronic Materials 12(5), 2026)
- Guo, Zhang & Huang, "Recent progress in organic optoelectronic synaptic transistor arrays" (Journal of Semiconductors 46(2), 2025) — directly relevant to organic CIM arrays
- Hoch et al., "Multifunctional Organic Materials for Neuromorphic Computing" (Nano-Micro Letters 17, 2025)
- Shan et al., "Organic Electrochemical Synaptic Transistors with Improved Retention" (Advanced Materials 38(4), 2026) — 82% retention at 1,000 s
- Won et al., "Enhancing Synaptic Plasticity and Multistate Retention of Organic Neuromorphic Devices" (Advanced Functional Materials 36(26), 2026) — σC2C = 0.96%

---

## Conclusion: key issues for the review

The manuscript's core contribution — the first profile-driven behavioral simulation bridging organic optoelectronic device characteristics with system-level DNN inference on modern architectures (Tiny-ViT, ConvNeXt, ResNet-18) — fills a **documented and genuine gap** that no existing CIM framework addresses. The ensemble HAT concept appears novel. However, five issues warrant serious attention in review:

**First**, the retention parameters (τ₁ = 140 ms, τ₂ = 610 ms) appear to conflate PPF short-term plasticity decay from Vincze et al. with CIM weight retention — a fundamental physical distinction. Real organic LTP retention is orders of magnitude longer (>60–1,000 s). **Second**, Vincze's device operates at 200 K, not ambient conditions, making its parameters inappropriate for an edge vision inference scenario without explicit justification. **Third**, the composite device profile draws from heterogeneous sources without demonstrating that these parameters coexist in any single device or operating condition. **Fourth**, the 76-percentage-point accuracy recovery from ensemble HAT is far larger than any reported HAT improvement in inorganic CIM (typically 1.5–4.4%), suggesting either genuinely novel effectiveness or an artificially harsh baseline. **Fifth**, the energy upper bound (11.45×) is plausible in simulation but should be benchmarked against IBM's actual hardware demonstrations (3–4× for transformers) and specify its digital baseline precisely. The paper should also cite NeuroSim V1.5's concurrent ViT support and the Rasch et al. 2023 HAT framework as essential context for positioning its contribution.
